class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_Simple_Zilla_Slab.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Zilla_Slab" title="Zilla Slab">Zilla Slab</a>, Mozilla\'s typeface since 2017</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Mozilla</b> (stylized as <b>moz://a</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a> community founded in 1998 by members of <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a>. The Mozilla community uses, develops, spreads and supports Mozilla products, thereby promoting exclusively free software and open standards, with only minor exceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The community is supported institutionally by the <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">not-for-profit</a> <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> and its tax-paying subsidiary, the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Corporation" title="Mozilla Corporation">Mozilla Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Mozilla_products" title="List of Mozilla products">Mozilla\'s current products</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> web browser, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Thunderbird</a> e-mail client (now through a subsidiary), <a href="/wiki/Bugzilla" title="Bugzilla">Bugzilla</a> bug tracking system, <a href="/wiki/Gecko_(software)" title="Gecko (software)">Gecko</a> layout engine, <a href="/wiki/Pocket_(service)" title="Pocket (service)">Pocket</a> "read-it-later-online" service, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 180P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;180p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;320&quot; src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/84/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm.240p.vp9.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Small VP9 (240P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 240P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;240p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;426&quot; src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/84/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm.240p.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Small WebM (240P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;WebM 240P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;240p.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;426&quot; data-height=&quot;240&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;325512&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:The Story of Mozilla by Mitchell Baker.webm" style="width:220px;height:124px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm/220px--The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Story_of_Mozilla_by_Mitchell_Baker.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Baker" title="Mitchell Baker">Mitchell Baker</a> telling the early history of Mozilla</div></div></div>\n<p>On January 23, 1998, Netscape made two announcements: first, that <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communicator" title="Netscape Communicator">Netscape Communicator</a> would be free; second, that the source code would also be free.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> One day later <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Zawinski" title="Jamie Zawinski">Jamie Zawinski</a>, from Netscape, registered <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886049734">.mw-parser-output .monospaced{font-family:monospace,monospace}</style><span class="monospaced">mozilla.org</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The project took its name, "Mozilla", after the original code name of the <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Navigator" title="Netscape Navigator">Netscape Navigator</a> browser\xe2\x80\x94a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Godzilla" title="Godzilla">Godzilla</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-google_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and used to co-ordinate the development of the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Application_Suite" title="Mozilla Application Suite">Mozilla Application Suite</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source</a> version of Netscape\'s internet software, <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communicator" title="Netscape Communicator">Netscape Communicator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mozilla_Launch_Announcement_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mozilla_Launch_Announcement-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Jamie Zawinski says he came up with the name "Mozilla" at a Netscape staff meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> A small group of Netscape employees were tasked with coordination of the new community.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png/220px-Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png/330px-Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png/440px-Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="929" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_dinosaur_head_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozilla\'s former symbol, as designed by <a href="/wiki/Shepard_Fairey" title="Shepard Fairey">Shepard Fairey</a> in 1998</div></div></div>\n<p>Originally, Mozilla aimed to be a technology provider for companies, such as Netscape, who would commercialize their open-source code.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a> (Netscape\'s parent company) greatly reduced its involvement with Mozilla in July 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> was designated the legal steward of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, Mozilla deprecated the Mozilla Suite in favor of creating independent applications for each function, primarily the <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> web browser and the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Thunderbird</a> email client, and moved to supply them directly to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mozilla\'s activities have since expanded to include Firefox on mobile platforms (primarily <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> a mobile OS called <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">Firefox OS</a> (since cancelled),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> a web-based identity system called <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Persona" title="Mozilla Persona">Mozilla Persona</a> and a marketplace for HTML5 applications.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a report released in November 2012, Mozilla reported that their total revenue for 2011 was $163&#160;million, which was up 33% from $123&#160;million in 2010. Mozilla noted that roughly 85% of their revenue comes from their contract with Google.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the end of 2013, Mozilla announced a deal with <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a> whereby Firefox would download and use a Cisco-provided binary build of an open-source<sup id="cite_ref-github_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-github-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Codec" title="Codec">codec</a> to play the <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_format" title="Proprietary format">proprietary</a> <a href="/wiki/H.264" class="mw-redirect" title="H.264">H.264</a> video format.<sup id="cite_ref-gigaom_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gigaom-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-techrepublic_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrepublic-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> As part of the deal, Cisco would pay any patent licensing fees associated with the binaries that it distributes. Mozilla\'s CTO, <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Eich" title="Brendan Eich">Brendan Eich</a>, acknowledged that this is "not a complete solution" and isn\'t "perfect".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> An employee in Mozilla\'s video formats team, writing in an unofficial capacity, justified<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> it by the need to maintain their large user base, which would be necessary in future battles for truly free video formats.\n</p><p>In December 2013, Mozilla announced funding for the development of non-<a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free</a> games<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> through its Game Creator Challenge. However, even those games that may be released under a non-free software or open-source license must be made with open web technologies and Javascript as per the work criteria outlined in the announcement.\n</p><p>In January 2017 the company rebranded away from its dinosaur symbol in favor of a logo that includes a "://" character sequence from a URL, with the revamped logo: "moz://a".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2020 Mozilla announced it would be cutting off 25% of its staff to reduce costs. Firefox has fallen from 30% market share to 4% in 10 years. Despite this executive pay has increased 400%, with <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Baker" title="Mitchell Baker">Mitchell Baker</a>, Mozilla\xe2\x80\x99s top executive, being paid $2.4m in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2020, Mozilla closed its <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View</a> office.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eich_CEO_promotion_controversy">Eich CEO promotion controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Eich CEO promotion controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On March 24, 2014, Mozilla promoted <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Eich" title="Brendan Eich">Brendan Eich</a> to the role of CEO. This led to boycotts and protests from the LGBT community and its supporters, as Eich previously donated US$1,000<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> of his own money in 2008 in support of <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8_(2008)" class="mw-redirect" title="California Proposition 8 (2008)">California\'s Proposition 8</a>, a California ballot proposition and state constitutional amendment in opposition to same-sex marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-arstechnica_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arstechnica-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Eich\'s donation first became public knowledge in 2012, while he was Mozilla\xe2\x80\x99s chief technical officer, leading to angry responses on Twitter\xe2\x80\x94including the use of the hashtag "#wontworkwithbigots".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Protests also emerged in 2014 following the announcement of Eich\'s appointment as CEO of Mozilla. U.S. companies <a href="/wiki/OkCupid" title="OkCupid">OkCupid</a> and <a href="/wiki/CREDO_Mobile" title="CREDO Mobile">CREDO Mobile</a> received media coverage for their objections, with the former asking its users to boycott the browser,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> while Credo amassed 50,000 signatures for a petition that called for Eich\'s resignation.\n</p><p>Due to the controversy, Eich voluntarily stepped down on April 3, 2014<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Baker" title="Mitchell Baker">Mitchell Baker</a>, executive chairwoman of Mozilla Corporation, posted a statement on the Mozilla blog: "We didn\'t move fast enough to engage with people once the controversy started. Mozilla believes both in equality and freedom of speech. Equality is necessary for meaningful speech. And you need free speech to fight for equality."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Eich\'s resignation promoted a backlash as he seemed to have been forced out of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>OkCupid co-founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Sam_Yagan" title="Sam Yagan">Sam Yagan</a> had also donated $500<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> to Republican candidate <a href="/wiki/Chris_Cannon" title="Chris Cannon">Chris Cannon</a> who proceeded to vote for multiple measures viewed as "anti-gay", including the banning of same-sex marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Yagan claims he did not know about Cannon\'s stance on gay rights and that his contribution was due to the candidate being the ranking Republican participating in the House subcommittee that oversaw Internet and Intellectual Property matters.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uncrunched.com_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uncrunched.com-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Reader comments on articles that were published close to the events were divided between support for OkCupid\'s actions and opposition to them. Supporters claimed the boycott was justified and saw OkCupid\'s actions as a firm statement of opposition to intolerance towards the gay community. Opponents saw OkCupid\'s actions as hypocritical, since Eich is also the inventor of <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Eich#Netscape_and_JavaScript" title="Brendan Eich">JavaScript</a>, which is still required to browse OkCupid\'s website, and felt that users should not be punished for the actions of Mozilla and suspected that OkCupid\'s actions were a <a href="/wiki/Publicity_stunt" title="Publicity stunt">publicity stunt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uncrunched.com_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uncrunched.com-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Values">Values</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Values">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_Manifesto">Mozilla Manifesto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mozilla Manifesto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Manifesto" title="Mozilla Manifesto">Mozilla Manifesto</a></div>\n<p>The Mozilla Manifesto outlines Mozilla\'s goals and principles.<sup id="cite_ref-manifesto_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manifesto-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> It asserts Mozilla\'s commitment to the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">internet</a>, saying: "The open, global internet is the most powerful communication and collaboration resource we have ever seen. It embodies some of our deepest hopes for human progress." It then outlines what Mozilla sees as its place in the development of the internet, stating "The Mozilla project uses a community-based approach to create world-class open source software and to develop new types of collaborative activities". And finally, it lays out their ten principles:\n</p>\n<ol><li>The internet is an integral part of modern life\xe2\x80\x94a key component in education, communication, collaboration, business, entertainment and society as a whole.</li>\n<li>The internet is a global public resource that must remain open and accessible.</li>\n<li>The internet must enrich the lives of individual human beings.</li>\n<li>Individuals\xe2\x80\x99 security and privacy on the internet are fundamental and must not be treated as optional.</li>\n<li>Individuals must have the ability to shape the internet and their own experiences on it.</li>\n<li>The effectiveness of the internet as a public resource depends upon interoperability (protocols, data formats, content), innovation and decentralized participation worldwide.</li>\n<li>Free and open source software promotes the development of the internet as a public resource.</li>\n<li>Transparent community-based processes promote participation, accountability and trust.</li>\n<li>Commercial involvement in the development of the internet brings many benefits; a balance between commercial profit and public benefit is critical.</li>\n<li>Magnifying the public benefit aspects of the internet is an important goal, worthy of time, attention and commitment.</li></ol>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pledge">Pledge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pledge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the Mozilla Foundation:<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Mozilla Foundation pledges to support the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Manifesto" title="Mozilla Manifesto">Mozilla Manifesto</a> in its activities. Specifically, we will:\n</p><ol><li>Build and enable open-source technologies and communities that support the Manifesto\xe2\x80\x99s principles;</li>\n<li>Build and deliver great consumer products that support the Manifesto\xe2\x80\x99s principles;</li>\n<li>Use the Mozilla assets (intellectual property such as copyrights and trademarks, infrastructure, funds, and reputation) to keep the Internet an open platform;</li>\n<li>Promote models for creating economic value for the public benefit; and</li>\n<li>Promote the Mozilla Manifesto principles in public discourse and within the Internet industry.</li></ol>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox">Firefox</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Firefox">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firefox_logo,_2019.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg/220px-Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg/330px-Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg/440px-Firefox_logo%2C_2019.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="87" data-file-height="82" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firefox_logo,_2019.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The revamped Firefox logo</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> is a family of <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a> products developed by Mozilla, with the <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox browser</a> as the flagship product.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_browser">Firefox browser</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Firefox browser">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> browser, or simply Firefox, is a <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a> and Mozilla\'s <a href="/wiki/Flagship_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagship product">flagship</a> software product. It is available in both desktop and mobile versions. Firefox uses the <a href="/wiki/Gecko_(software)" title="Gecko (software)">Gecko</a> <a href="/wiki/Browser_engine" title="Browser engine">layout engine</a> to render web pages, which implements current and anticipated <a href="/wiki/Web_standards" title="Web standards">web standards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> As of late 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Firefox had approximately 10-11% of worldwide <a href="/wiki/Usage_share_of_web_browsers#Summary" title="Usage share of web browsers">usage share of web browsers</a>, making it the 4th most-used web browser.<sup id="cite_ref-w3counter1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3counter1-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gs.statcounter.com_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gs.statcounter.com-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-getclicky1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-getclicky1-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Firefox began as an experimental branch of the Mozilla codebase by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Hyatt" title="Dave Hyatt">Dave Hyatt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hewitt_(programmer)" title="Joe Hewitt (programmer)">Joe Hewitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blake_Ross" title="Blake Ross">Blake Ross</a>. They believed the commercial requirements of <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a>\'s sponsorship and developer-driven <a href="/wiki/Feature_creep" title="Feature creep">feature creep</a> compromised the utility of the Mozilla browser.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> To combat what they saw as the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Application_Suite" title="Mozilla Application Suite">Mozilla Suite\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Software_bloat" title="Software bloat">software bloat</a>, they created a stand-alone browser, with which they intended to replace the Mozilla Suite.\n</p><p>Firefox was originally named <i>Phoenix</i> but the name was changed so as to avoid trademark conflicts with <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Technologies" title="Phoenix Technologies">Phoenix Technologies</a>. The initially-announced replacement, <i>Firebird</i>, provoked objections from the <a href="/wiki/Firebird_(database_server)" title="Firebird (database server)">Firebird</a> project community.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The current name, Firefox, was chosen on February 9, 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has been announced that Mozilla is going to launch a premium version of the Firefox browser by October 2019. The company\'s CEO, Chris Beard, has been quoted by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Web" class="mw-redirect" title="The Next Web">The Next Web</a></i> to say that "there is no plan to charge money for things that are now free. So we will roll out a subscription service and offer a premium level."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_for_mobile">Firefox for mobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Firefox for mobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_for_Android" title="Firefox for Android">Firefox for Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/Firefox_for_iOS" title="Firefox for iOS">Firefox for iOS</a></div>\n<p>Firefox for mobile (codenamed <i>Fennec</i>) is the build of the <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Mozilla Firefox</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a> for mobile devices such as <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>. Initially available on multiple platforms, it is now available in two versions: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_for_Android" title="Firefox for Android">Firefox for Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/Firefox_for_iOS" title="Firefox for iOS">Firefox for iOS</a>. Firefox for Android runs on the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating system</a> and uses the same <a href="/wiki/Gecko_(software)" title="Gecko (software)">Gecko</a> <a href="/wiki/Browser_engine" title="Browser engine">layout engine</a> as <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Mozilla Firefox</a>; for example, version 1.0 used the same engine as Firefox 3.6, and the following release, 4.0, shared core code with Firefox 4.0. Firefox for iOS, which runs on the <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> mobile operating system, does not use the Gecko Layout Engine because of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>\'s policy that all iOS apps that browse the web must use the built-in iOS <a href="/wiki/WebKit" title="WebKit">WebKit</a> rendering engine.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Both version include features like <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> support, <a href="/wiki/Firefox_Sync" title="Firefox Sync">Firefox Sync</a>, <a href="/wiki/Private_browsing" title="Private browsing">private browsing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_tracking" title="Web tracking">web tracking</a> protection, and <a href="/wiki/Tab_(interface)" title="Tab (interface)">tabbed browsing</a>, and Firefox for Android also includes support for <a href="/wiki/Add-on_(Mozilla)" title="Add-on (Mozilla)">add-ons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Focus">Firefox Focus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Firefox Focus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_Focus" title="Firefox Focus">Firefox Focus</a></div>\n<p>Firefox Focus is a free and open-source privacy-focused <a href="/wiki/Mobile_browser" title="Mobile browser">mobile browser</a> for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Initially released in 2015 as only a <a href="/wiki/Web_tracking" title="Web tracking">tracker</a>-blocking application for iOS, it has since been developed into a full mobile browser for both iOS and Android.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Lockwise">Firefox Lockwise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Firefox Lockwise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_Lockwise" title="Firefox Lockwise">Firefox Lockwise</a></div>\n<p>Firefox Lockwise is a <a href="/wiki/Password_manager" title="Password manager">password manager</a> offered by Mozilla.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On desktop, it is a built-in feature of the <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> browser. On mobile, it is offered as a standalone app that can be set as the device\'s default password manager.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Monitor">Firefox Monitor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Firefox Monitor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_Monitor" title="Firefox Monitor">Firefox Monitor</a></div>\n<p>Firefox Monitor is an online service that informs users if their <a href="/wiki/Email_address" title="Email address">email address</a> and <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">passwords</a> have been leaked in <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breaches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Send">Firefox Send</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Firefox Send">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_Send" title="Firefox Send">Firefox Send</a></div>\n<p>Firefox Send was an online <a href="/wiki/Encrypted" class="mw-redirect" title="Encrypted">encrypted</a> <a href="/wiki/File_sharing" title="File sharing">file-transfer</a> service offered by Mozilla.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In September 2020, Mozilla announced that Firefox Send will be decommissioned and will no longer be part of the product lineup.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_VPN">Mozilla VPN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mozilla VPN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_VPN" title="Mozilla VPN">Mozilla VPN</a></div>\n<p>Mozilla VPN, formerly Firefox Private Network, is a subscription-based <a href="/wiki/VPN" class="mw-redirect" title="VPN">VPN</a> and a free privacy extension.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Private_Relay">Firefox Private Relay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Firefox Private Relay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Firefox Private Relay provides users with <a href="/wiki/Disposable_email_address" title="Disposable email address">disposable email addresses</a> that can be used to combat spam (by hiding user\'s real email address) and manage email subscriptions by categorizing them based on the party a particular address was given to.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_Reality">Firefox Reality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Firefox Reality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In September 2018, Mozilla announced that its VR version was ready for consumers to download. Called Firefox Reality, the browser was built entirely for virtual reality. It is currently available on the <a href="/wiki/Oculus_Rift" title="Oculus Rift">Oculus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2019, HTC also announced its partnership with Mozilla. Under the partnership, Firefox Reality web browser has been made available on the Vive headsets.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_OS">Firefox OS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Firefox OS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">Firefox OS</a></div>\n<p>Firefox OS (project name: <i>Boot to Gecko</i> also known as <i>B2G</i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> that was developed by Mozilla to support <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> apps written using "<a href="/wiki/Web_standards" title="Web standards">open Web</a>" technologies rather than platform-specific native <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">APIs</a>. The concept behind Firefox OS is that all user-accessible software will be HTML5 applications, that use Open Web APIs to access the phone\'s hardware directly via <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some devices using this OS include<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Alcatel One Touch Fire, ZTE Open, and LG Fireweb. Mozilla announced the end of Firefox OS development in December 2015.\n</p><p>A fork of B2G, <a href="/wiki/KaiOS" title="KaiOS">KaiOS</a>, has continued development and ships with numerous low-cost devices.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pocket">Pocket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Pocket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pocket_(service)" title="Pocket (service)">Pocket (service)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pocket_App_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pocket_App_Logo.png/220px-Pocket_App_Logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="56" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pocket_App_Logo.png/330px-Pocket_App_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pocket_App_Logo.png/440px-Pocket_App_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="1103" data-file-height="282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pocket_App_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Pocket app logo</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pocket_(service)" title="Pocket (service)">Pocket</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_application" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile application">mobile application</a> and <a href="/wiki/Web_service" title="Web service">web service</a> for managing a reading list of articles from the Internet. It was announced that it would be acquired by the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Corporation" title="Mozilla Corporation">Mozilla Corporation</a>, the commercial arm of Mozilla\'s <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">non-profit</a> development group, on February 27, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Originally designed only for desktop browsers,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> it is now available for <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kobo_eReader" title="Kobo eReader">Kobo eReaders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thunderbird">Thunderbird</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Thunderbird">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Mozilla Thunderbird</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Thunderbird</a> is a free, open-source, cross-platform email and news client developed by the volunteers of the Mozilla Community.\n</p><p>On July 16, 2012, Mitchell Baker announced that Mozilla\'s leadership had come to the conclusion that on-going stability was the most important thing for Thunderbird and that innovation in Thunderbird was no longer a priority for Mozilla. In that update Baker also suggested that Mozilla had provided a pathway for its community to innovate around Thunderbird if the community chooses.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SeaMonkey">SeaMonkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: SeaMonkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/SeaMonkey" title="SeaMonkey">SeaMonkey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:130px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SeaMonkey.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/SeaMonkey.png" decoding="async" width="128" height="128" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SeaMonkey.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>SeaMonkey logo</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/SeaMonkey" title="SeaMonkey">SeaMonkey</a> (formerly the Mozilla Application Suite) is a free and open-source cross platform suite of Internet software components including a web browser component, a client for sending and receiving email and <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">Usenet</a> newsgroup messages, an HTML editor (<a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Composer" title="Mozilla Composer">Mozilla Composer</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/ChatZilla" title="ChatZilla">ChatZilla</a> IRC client.\n</p><p>On March 10, 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> announced that it would not release any official versions of Mozilla Application Suite beyond 1.7.x, since it had now focused on the stand-alone applications <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Thunderbird</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> SeaMonkey is now maintained by the SeaMonkey Council, which has <a href="/wiki/Trademark" title="Trademark">trademarked</a> the SeaMonkey name with help from the Mozilla Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Mozilla Foundation provides project hosting for the SeaMonkey developers.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bugzilla">Bugzilla</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bugzilla">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bugzilla" title="Bugzilla">Bugzilla</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Buggie.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Buggie.svg/220px-Buggie.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Buggie.svg/330px-Buggie.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Buggie.svg/440px-Buggie.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="95" data-file-height="125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Buggie.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bugzilla logo</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bugzilla" title="Bugzilla">Bugzilla</a> is a <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">web</a>-based general-purpose <a href="/wiki/Bug_tracking_system" title="Bug tracking system">bug tracking system</a>, which was released as <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a> by <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Netscape Communications">Netscape Communications</a> in 1998 along with the rest of the Mozilla codebase, and is currently stewarded by Mozilla. It has been adopted by a variety of organizations for use as a <a href="/wiki/Bug_tracking_system" title="Bug tracking system">bug tracking system</a> for both <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary</a> projects and products, including the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a>, <a href="/wiki/GNOME" title="GNOME">GNOME</a>, <a href="/wiki/KDE" title="KDE">KDE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">Red Hat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">Novell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse</a> and <a href="/wiki/LibreOffice" title="LibreOffice">LibreOffice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Components">Components</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Components">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="NSS">NSS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: NSS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Network_Security_Services" title="Network Security Services">Network Security Services</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Network_Security_Services" title="Network Security Services">Network Security Services</a> (NSS) comprises a set of <a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)" title="Library (computing)">libraries</a> designed to support <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross-platform">cross-platform</a> development of security-enabled client and server applications. NSS provides a complete open-source implementation of crypto libraries supporting <a href="/wiki/Secure_Sockets_Layer" class="mw-redirect" title="Secure Sockets Layer">SSL</a> and <a href="/wiki/S/MIME" title="S/MIME">S/MIME</a>. NSS is licensed under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GPL</a>-compatible <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Public_License" title="Mozilla Public License">Mozilla Public License</a> 2.0.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">Red Hat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>/<a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and other companies and individual contributors have co-developed NSS and it is used in a wide range of non-Mozilla products including <a href="/wiki/Evolution_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolution (software)">Evolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pidgin_(software)" title="Pidgin (software)">Pidgin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LibreOffice" title="LibreOffice">LibreOffice</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="SpiderMonkey">SpiderMonkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: SpiderMonkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/SpiderMonkey_(JavaScript_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="SpiderMonkey (JavaScript engine)">SpiderMonkey (JavaScript engine)</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/SpiderMonkey_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="SpiderMonkey (software)">SpiderMonkey</a> is the original <a href="/wiki/JavaScript_engine" title="JavaScript engine">JavaScript engine</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Eich" title="Brendan Eich">Brendan Eich</a> when he invented <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> in 1995 as a developer at <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a>. It became part of the Mozilla product family when Mozilla inherited Netscape\'s code-base in 1998. In 2011, Eich transferred the nominal ownership of the SpiderMonkey code and project to Dave Mandelin.<sup id="cite_ref-BE201106_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BE201106-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>SpiderMonkey is a <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross-platform">cross-platform</a> engine written in <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> which implements <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a>, a standard developed from JavaScript.<sup id="cite_ref-BE201106_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BE201106-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> It comprises an <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreter</a>, several <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compilation" title="Just-in-time compilation">just-in-time compilers</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Decompiler" title="Decompiler">decompiler</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Garbage_collection_(computer_science)" title="Garbage collection (computer science)">garbage collector</a>. Products which embed SpiderMonkey include <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Thunderbird" title="Mozilla Thunderbird">Thunderbird</a>, <a href="/wiki/SeaMonkey" title="SeaMonkey">SeaMonkey</a>, and many non-Mozilla applications.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhino">Rhino</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Rhino">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rhino_(JavaScript_engine)" title="Rhino (JavaScript engine)">Rhino (JavaScript engine)</a></div>\n<p>Rhino is an <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source</a> <a href="/wiki/JavaScript_engine" title="JavaScript engine">JavaScript engine</a> managed by the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a>. It is developed entirely in <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>. Rhino converts JavaScript scripts into Java <a href="/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)" title="Class (computer programming)">classes</a>. Rhino works in both <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compiled</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreted</a> mode.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gecko">Gecko</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Gecko">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gecko_(software)" title="Gecko (software)">Gecko (software)</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gecko_(software)" title="Gecko (software)">Gecko</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Browser_engine" title="Browser engine">layout engine</a> that supports web pages written using <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">SVG</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MathML" title="MathML">MathML</a>. Gecko is written in <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> and uses <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Portable_Runtime" title="Netscape Portable Runtime">NSPR</a> for <a href="/wiki/Platform_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Platform independence">platform independence</a>. Its source code is licensed under the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Public_License" title="Mozilla Public License">Mozilla Public License</a>.\n</p><p>Firefox uses Gecko both for rendering web pages and for rendering its <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a>. Gecko is also used by Thunderbird, SeaMonkey, and many non-Mozilla applications.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rust">Rust</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rust">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rust_(programming_language)" title="Rust (programming language)">Rust (programming language)</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rust_(programming_language)" title="Rust (programming language)">Rust</a> is a compiled <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming language</a> being developed by Mozilla Research. It is designed for safety, concurrency, and performance. Rust is intended for creating large and complex software which needs to be both safe against exploits and fast.\n</p><p>Rust is being used in an experimental layout engine, <a href="/wiki/Servo_(layout_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Servo (layout engine)">Servo</a>, which was developed by Mozilla and Samsung. Servo is not used in any consumer-oriented browsers yet. However, the Servo project developers plan for parts of the Servo source code to be merged into Gecko, and Firefox, incrementally.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="XULRunner">XULRunner</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: XULRunner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/XULRunner" title="XULRunner">XULRunner</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/XULRunner" title="XULRunner">XULRunner</a> is a software platform and technology experiment by Mozilla, that allows applications built with the same technologies used by Firefox extensions (XPCOM, Javascript, HTML, CSS, XUL) to be run natively as desktop applications, without requiring Firefox to be installed on the user\'s machine. XULRunner binaries are available for the Windows, Linux and OS X operating systems, allowing such applications to be effectively cross-platform.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="pdf.js">pdf.js</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: pdf.js">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pdf.js" class="mw-redirect" title="Pdf.js">pdf.js</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pdf.js" class="mw-redirect" title="Pdf.js">Pdf.js</a> is a library developed by Mozilla that allows in-browser rendering of pdf documents using the HTML5 Canvas and JavaScript. It is included by default in Firefox, allowing the browser to render pdf documents without requiring an external plugin; and it is available separately as an extension named "PDF Viewer" for Firefox for Android, SeaMonkey, and the Firefox versions which don\'t include it built-in. It can also be included as part of a website\'s scripts, to allow pdf rendering for any browser that implements the required HTML5 features and can run JavaScript.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shumway">Shumway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Shumway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shumway_(software)" title="Shumway (software)">Shumway (software)</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Shumway_(software)" title="Shumway (software)">Shumway</a> is an open-source replacement for the Adobe Flash Player, developed by Mozilla since 2012, using open web technologies as a replacement for Flash technologies. It uses Javascript and HTML5 Canvas elements to render Flash and execute Actionscript. It is included by default in Firefox Nightly and can be installed as an extension for any recent version of Firefox. The current implementation is limited in its capabilities to render Flash content outside simple projects.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Servo">Servo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Servo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Servo_(software)" title="Servo (software)">Servo (software)</a></div>\n<p>Servo is a browser engine being developed for application and embedded use.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In August 2020, during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, due to lack of funds and organization restructuring, Mozilla laid off most of the Servo development team. The team was disbanded.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf/page1-220px-Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf/page1-330px-Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf/page1-440px-Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="873" data-file-height="1329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_-_Internet_Health_Report_2019.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozilla engages in social outreach about user rights on the Internet. This 2019 Internet Health Report is their guide to their understanding of the state of the Internet.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_VR">Mozilla VR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mozilla VR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mozilla VR is a team focused on bringing <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> (VR) tools, specifications, and standards to the open Web.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Mozilla VR maintains <a href="/wiki/A-Frame_(virtual_reality_framework)" title="A-Frame (virtual reality framework)">A-Frame (VR)</a>, a web framework for building VR experiences, and works on advancing <a href="/wiki/WebVR" title="WebVR">WebVR</a> support within web browsers.\n</p><p>On April 26, 2018, the first experiment from their Social Mixed Reality efforts was released; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://hubs.mozilla.com/">Hubs</a>, a multi-user virtual space in <a href="/wiki/WebVR" title="WebVR">WebVR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_Persona">Mozilla Persona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Mozilla Persona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Persona" title="Mozilla Persona">Mozilla Persona</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Persona" title="Mozilla Persona">Mozilla Persona</a> was a secure, cross-browser website <a href="/wiki/Authentication" title="Authentication">authentication</a> mechanism which allowed a user to use a single username and password (or other authentication method) to log into multiple sites.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Mozilla Persona shut down on November 30, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_Location_Service">Mozilla Location Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Mozilla Location Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Location_Service" title="Mozilla Location Service">Mozilla Location Service</a></div>\n<p>This open-source crowdsourced geolocation service was started by Mozilla in 2013 and offers a free <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">API</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Webmaker">Webmaker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Webmaker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mozilla Webmaker is Mozilla\'s educational initiative, and Webmaker\'s goal is to "help millions of people move from using the web to making the web." As part of Mozilla\'s non-profit mission, Webmaker aims "to help the world increase their understanding of the web, take greater control of their online lives, and create a more web literate planet."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lifehacker.com_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifehacker.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MDN_Web_Docs">MDN Web Docs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: MDN Web Docs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/MDN_Web_Docs" title="MDN Web Docs">MDN Web Docs</a></div>\n<p>Mozilla maintains a comprehensive developer documentation website called the <a href="/wiki/MDN_Web_Docs" title="MDN Web Docs">MDN Web Docs</a> which contains information about web technologies including <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">SVG</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, as well as Mozilla-specific information. In addition, Mozilla publishes a large number of videos about web technologies and the development of Mozilla projects on the Air Mozilla website.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_Voice">Common Voice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Common Voice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Common_Voice" title="Common Voice">Common Voice</a></div>\n<p>In July 2017, Mozilla launched the project <a href="/wiki/Common_Voice" title="Common Voice">Common Voice</a> to help make voice recognition open to everyone.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Visitors to the website can donate their voice to help build an open-source voice recognition engine that anyone can use to make apps for devices and the web that make use of voice recognition. The website allows visitors to read a sentence to help the machine system learn how real people speak, as well as validate the read sentences of other people.\n</p><p>Mozilla publishes Common Voice data sets under a <a href="/wiki/CC-0" class="mw-redirect" title="CC-0">CC-0</a> license.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="IRL_.E2.80.93_Online_Life_Is_Real_Life"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="IRL_\xe2\x80\x93_Online_Life_Is_Real_Life">IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IRL_%E2%80%93_Online_Life_Is_Real_Life" title="IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life">IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life</a></div>\n<p>On June 26, 2017, Mozilla launched <i><a href="/wiki/IRL_%E2%80%93_Online_Life_Is_Real_Life" title="IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life">IRL \xe2\x80\x93 Online Life Is Real Life</a></i> to explore popular stories from the web that deal with issues of the internet that affect society as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community">Community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Mozilla Community consists of over 40,000 active contributors from across the globe<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. It includes both paid employees and volunteers who work towards the goals set forth<sup id="cite_ref-manifesto_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manifesto-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Manifesto" title="Mozilla Manifesto">Mozilla Manifesto</a>. Many of the sub-communities in Mozilla have formed around localization efforts for Mozilla Firefox, and the Mozilla web properties.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_communities">Local communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Local communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg/220px-London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg/330px-London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg/440px-London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Mozilla_Workspace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozilla spaces, London</div></div></div>\n<p>There are a number of sub-communities that exist based on their geographical locations, where contributors near each other work together on particular activities, such as localization, marketing, PR and user support.\n</p><p>In 2017, Mozilla created a Wireless Innovation for Network Security (WINS)<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> challenge that awarded a total of $2 million in prize money to innovators who used its decentralized design to create wireless solutions for post-natural disaster internet access.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This challenge also envisioned to connect communities which lacked internet access.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_Reps">Mozilla Reps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Mozilla Reps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg/220px-Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg/330px-Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg/440px-Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozilla_Reps_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozilla Reps logo</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mozilla Reps program is a volunteer-based program, which allows volunteers to become official representatives of Mozilla. Volunteers are required to be 18 years or older in order to participate in the program.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Activities under the program include recruitment for contributors, workshops, and attending Mozilla summits.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences_and_events">Conferences and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Conferences and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozilla_Festival">Mozilla Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Mozilla Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="box-Multiple_issues plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-multiple_issues compact-ambox" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><div class="mw-collapsible" style="width:95%; class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fireside_Chat,_Knight%27s_Michael_Maness_and_Dan_Sinker_-_Flickr_-_Knight_Foundation.jpg" class="image"><img 1.5x,
